<user>111711797880452354333<//user><name>Cassidy Byrd< /name><date>1524088832977<//date><Rate>5<//Rate>< review>
The vegetarian ramen was great- not too salty, bold flavor. Lots of noodles and toppings... But let's be real- this review is for the tempura egg. DAMN. Not since Hawaii have I experienced one as perfected as this. These are magical. The outside had the thinnest crisp of the fryer process, and the inside firm, but soft enough that if you were toothless, you could enjoy it just as much since it practically melts in your mouth. The gooey center when turned upside down was thick enough to be a slow crawl out of its warm white crown. Would drive from San Jose just to get an order of 5-6 of these.<//review>

< Text>
Do not understand why people giving this place 4 or 5 stars for ok ramen. This place is just ok. I had the chicken karaage ramen and broth was super light. Yes its a soy broth ramen but it tasted bland. Mostly just added spicy oil over it. They only give you half a boil egg and sprouts as well. It is missing bamboo shoots, mushroom, scallions and even sea weed. Perhaps the skewed meats would be a better choice. It is also pricey for an ok place. My friend had the spicy miso ramen expecting thin slices of chasu pork but instead got cut up pieces of pork. The pork was mostly fatty parts and seemed like it was boiled and not roasted for hours. Its also a bit pricey for these types of ramen. The creations are a bit weird. Music playing in background are pop music and a bit loud. $19 for a pitcher of Sapporro? <user_id>110874177457784849782<//user_id><Name>Nick Contini</Name><Date>1530341916896<//Date><Rate>4</Rate>< text>
I enjoyed this place a lot! It strays a lot from traditional Japanese, but I thought the liberties taken felt mostly appropriate and made it a must try. The edmame was great. The karaage ramen was fantastic. I am, however disappointed in the KO ramen (their version of tonkotsu ramen). The ribs did not taste very marinated and the eggs were not marinated at all! That's two of the most important elements of tonkotsu ramen! The noodles, pork belly, and broth we're all still very rich and delicious, so still a good dish. I was also disappointed in the gyudon, since the rice was purely white, meaning bit didn't have any of that delicious broth soaked into it. The onions were also undercooked. The flavor of the beef was still sweet and scrumptious though. I got the vibe that the restaurant's less traditional dishes are where it shines. I'd definitely try it again.</text>

< rating>
4< /rating>
<Pictures>None</Pictures>< review>
4/5 Stars in 2017: Kaiju has definitely improved on food and service. Fusion ramen was pretty good, especially for a neighborhood joint. Prices seem high, but reasonable considering ingredients and the size of each bowl. Happy hour deals look good too.

2/5 Stars in 2015: Perhaps it was just bad timing and too high of expectations, but I came here and had a less than mediocre experience. Came here on a Sunday afternoon around 1pm by myself with no lines and no wait. Having heard that the fusion ramen was amazing, and seeing as the weather was a drizzly, I was more than ecstatic to try this place. Unfortunately, according to the staff, they ran out of many if the seafood and their shipment had not arrived yet, so there were no oysters, no uni, and no crab or lobster for the lobster tail and crab leg ramen. After all of my top choices were shot down, I opted for the Wasabi Chirashi, made tempting by their facebook cover photo. Unfortunately, since there was a lack of seafood, my chirashi had a few missing ingredients. The fish didn't seem too fresh, but by this point, my tummy was too hungry to argue with my brain. About half way through my meal, the kind waitress remembered she didn't serve me any tea or water, even though the place didn't get any busier after I had arrived.

Overall, meal was mediocre, though my disappointment may be heavily biased on my eagerness to try the ramen here... I'll give this place another try perhaps, though probably not anytime in the near future.<//review>

< Text>
I went Sunday after 7pm. this place is not a big place. maybe 10 tables. it was almost packed but maybe I came good time in a day. right away, seated and ordered in 2 mins. I ordered tataki (seared white tuna) and asari (clam with soy based broth) tataki came on hot plate which I haven't seen it served that way before. they put crispy rice between and source they put taste really good. not sure if white tuna is super fresh since tataki is supposed to be seared but taste good! asari ramen was delicious too. soup taste light. not too oily like tonkotsu. not no-taste like shio. just about right. lots of clams on top. usually these kinda thing, it's hide and seek. you really need to find clams underneath off noodle or hiding under seaweed but here it's carpet of clams. you see them there surely. only one thing, made me waaat? is noodle. I know there are many ramen noodle types and this one is good with miso broth kinda thing but what I found in my asari ramen was spaghetti. well, it wasn't pasta but I saw spaghetti in my ramen. I tasted spaghetti in my ramen. I had spaghetti with chopsticks. it was almost they are closing but the server wasn't pushy like "eat-leave-dont-review-us-here-but-5-stars-please." she was nice (but seemed wanna get off work right now.) I definitely come back there. it was delicious!<//Text>

< text>
It's a post office, folks. If it were all glamorous you would complain about the feds squandering our tax dollars. Its functional and the people who work there are polite and doing their best to keep up with the work load. My favorite service (which doesnt seem to be available all the time) is when the clerks come out to the lobby with the portable scanner. < review>
This place was ONCE, a long time ago, a nice and friendly place to do laundry.  Now they have 12 year old staff who are rude, 'bitchy but with a smile', and open and close the place whenever they feel like it.  It makes you wonder if there is a Owner/Manager at all.

As an example, I had put two loads of laundry in at 6:40 PM and still had 2 more to start.  At 7:02 PM, as a courtesy, I asked the 12 year old they had on duty if I could still start my other 2 loads.  She looked at me and with a huge fake smile said "The last loads have to be in by 7:00 PM."  I told her they were short washes, and pointed out that with 20 min to wash and 30 to dry that I'd be out by 7:45 PM.  She simply said "The last loads have to be in by 7:00 pm and anyway, I'm closing early tonight."

So apparently the teenage staff get to choose when they open and close based on how tired they are or their social schedule for that evening.  That's a pretty shi#%y way to run a business.

To make my irritation clear to this teenager, even knowing she was wanting "to leave early", I stayed until exactly 8:00 PM  and folded every item of my laundry, even with her asking me when I wold be done and her pacing around the place impatiently waiting for me to leave.

As a general business practice, if your posted business hours are 7:00 AM to 8:00 PM then you should hire responsible people who can tell time and not rush paying customers out of the place early just so they can duck out ahead of time to party on a Friday night!

A warning to all - - double check the hours for that day before you go, as you start your laundry and during the washing and drying cycles because these children they have running the place make up the hours as the night goes along.

Thankfully I found a MUCH better laundromat just a few miles away with vending machines, a swamp cooler, and a TV.  Look up Thrifty Wash at Rimrock Center on Hwy 111, near Gene Autry.  MUCH better facility!!!</review>

< Text>
Horrendously slow service.

I have been a long-time customer of Sears automotive in several states and have had excellent service before moving to Clovis.  It was because of this past positive experience that I continued to take my car to the Clovis Sears

I have dealt with this particular Sears several times in the past year, and each time the service is ridiculously slow.  Unfortunately there is no advantage to making an appointment as walk-ins are given equal priority and quoted similar wait times.  Clearly they know how to take an appointment, they just don't know how to honor the appointments.

A customer should never have to wait in line for over 30 minutes before being waited on.  And it should never take 2 hours to simply change oil.  Overall 2:30 is a horrendously unreasonable amount of time to get oil changed.

It is safe to say that I have given them the benefit of the doubt long enough and will be doing my business elsewhere from now on.</Text>
